However, there is a critical issue regarding the anomaly detection logic in the `SurveillanceGUI` class. The `is_anomaly` method currently uses a placeholder logic (`result > 0.5`) to determine if an anomaly is detected. This logic is too simplistic and does not reflect the actual behavior analysis required for identifying anomalies like loitering or erratic movement.

To address this, you should implement a more robust anomaly detection mechanism based on the output of the behavior analysis model. This could involve setting thresholds based on model outputs, using statistical methods, or employing additional machine learning techniques to classify behaviors as normal or anomalous.

   - Define clear criteria or thresholds for what constitutes an anomaly based on the model's output.
   - Consider using additional data or features if necessary to improve the accuracy of anomaly detection.

2. **Update the `is_anomaly` Method:**
   - Replace the placeholder logic with the newly defined criteria for anomaly detection.

By implementing these changes, the system will be better equipped to accurately identify anomalies and meet the user's requirements for behavior analysis."

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms

class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])

    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output

    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix

class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device

    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds

    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion

    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

from flask import Flask, render_template

app = Flask(__name__)

@app.route('/')
def index():
    # Render the main dashboard page
    return render_template('index.html')

def run_dashboard():
    app.run(host='0.0.0.0', port=5000)

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix

class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device

    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds

    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion

    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

'''
Main entry point for the AI surveillance solution.
'''
from video_stream_handler import VideoStreamHandler
from behavior_analyzer import BehaviorAnalyzer
from alert_system import AlertSystem
from web_dashboard import run_dashboard
from gui import SurveillanceGUI
def main():
    # Initialize components
    video_handler = VideoStreamHandler(rtsp_url="rtsp://your_stream_url")
    analyzer = BehaviorAnalyzer(model_path="model.pth")
    email_config = {
        'from': 'your_email@example.com',
        'to': 'recipient_email@example.com',
        'smtp_server': 'smtp.example.com',
        'smtp_port': 587,
        'username': 'your_username',
        'password': 'your_password'
    }
    alert_system = AlertSystem(email_config=email_config, push_service_url="http://push_service_url")
    # Start the web dashboard
    run_dashboard()
    # Start the GUI
    gui = SurveillanceGUI(video_handler, analyzer, alert_system)
    gui.run()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt
# Make port 5000 available to the world outside this container
EXPOSE 5000
# Run the application
CMD ["python", "main.py"]
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

'''

import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()

[]\n        with torch.no_grad():\n            for data in self.dataloader:\n                inputs, labels = data\n                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)\n ```python
'''
Main entry point for the AI surveillance solution.
'''
from video_stream_handler import VideoStreamHandler
from behavior_analyzer import BehaviorAnalyzer
from alert_system import AlertSystem
from web_dashboard import run_dashboard
from gui import SurveillanceGUI
def main():
    # Initialize components
    video_handler = VideoStreamHandler(rtsp_url="rtsp://your_stream_url")
    analyzer = BehaviorAnalyzer(model_path="model.pth")
    email_config = {
        'from': 'your_email@example.com',
        'to': 'recipient_email@example.com',
        'smtp_server': 'smtp.example.com',
        'smtp_port': 587,
        'username': 'your_username',
        'password': 'your_password'
    }
    alert_system = AlertSystem(email_config=email_config, push_service_url="http://push_service_url")
    # Start the web dashboard
    run_dashboard()
    # Start the GUI
    gui = SurveillanceGUI(video_handler, analyzer, alert_system)
    gui.run()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

```python
'''
Main entry point for the AI surveillance solution.
'''
from video_stream_handler import VideoStreamHandler
from behavior_analyzer import BehaviorAnalyzer
from alert_system import AlertSystem
from web_dashboard import run_dashboard
from gui import SurveillanceGUI
def main():
    # Initialize components
    video_handler = VideoStreamHandler(rtsp_url="rtsp://your_stream_url")
    analyzer = BehaviorAnalyzer(model_path="model.pth")
    email_config = {
        'from': 'your_email@example.com',
        'to': 'recipient_email@example.com',
        'smtp_server': 'smtp.example.com',
        'smtp_port': 587,
        'username': 'your_username',
        'password': 'your_password'
    }
    alert_system = AlertSystem(email_config=email_config, push_service_url="http://push_service_url")
    # Start the web dashboard
    run_dashboard()
    # Start the GUI
    gui = SurveillanceGUI(video_handler, analyzer, alert_system)
    gui.run()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```
behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```
alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```
gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

Main entry point for the AI surveillance solution.

from video_stream_handler import VideoStreamHandler
from behavior_analyzer import BehaviorAnalyzer

from gui import SurveillanceGUI
def main():
    # Initialize components
    video_handler = VideoStreamHandler(rtsp_url="rtsp://your_stream_url")
    analyzer = BehaviorAnalyzer(model_path="model.pth")
    email_config = {
        'from': 'your_email@example.com',
        'to': 'recipient_email@example.com',
        'smtp_server': 'smtp.example.com',

video_stream_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles RTSP video stream processing.
'''
import cv2
class VideoStreamHandler:
    def __init__(self, rtsp_url=""):
        self.rtsp_url = rtsp_url
        self.capture = cv2.VideoCapture(rtsp_url)
    def get_frame(self):
        ret, frame = self.capture.read()
        if not ret:
            raise Exception("Failed to capture video frame.")
        return frame
    def release(self):
        self.capture.release()
```

behavior_analyzer.py
```python
'''
Analyzes video frames for anomalies using a pre-trained model.
'''
import torch
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
class BehaviorAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, model_path="model.pth"):
        self.model = torch.load(model_path)
        self.model.eval()
        self.transform = transforms.Compose([
            transforms.ToTensor(),
            transforms.Resize((224, 224))
        ])
    def analyze_frame(self, frame):
        input_tensor = self.transform(frame).unsqueeze(0)
        with torch.no_grad():
            output = self.model(input_tensor)
        return output
    def is_anomaly(self, output):
        # Implement robust anomaly detection logic
        # Example: Assume output is a probability distribution over classes
        anomaly_threshold = 0.7  # Example threshold
        anomaly_score = output.max().item()  # Get the highest probability
        return anomaly_score < anomaly_threshold
```

alert_system.py
```python
'''
Manages alert notifications via email, push notifications, and dashboard updates.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
import requests
class AlertSystem:
    def __init__(self, email_config, push_service_url):
        self.email_config = email_config
        self.push_service_url = push_service_url
    def send_email(self, subject, message):
        msg = MIMEText(message)
        msg['Subject'] = subject
        msg['From'] = self.email_config['from']
        msg['To'] = self.email_config['to']
        with smtplib.SMTP(self.email_config['smtp_server'], self.email_config['smtp_port']) as server:
            server.login(self.email_config['username'], self.email_config['password'])
            server.send_message(msg)
    def send_push_notification(self, message):
        payload = {'message': message}
        response = requests.post(self.push_service_url, json=payload)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to send push notification.")
    def update_dashboard(self, alert_data):
        # Assuming the dashboard has an endpoint to receive updates
        dashboard_update_url = "http://localhost:5000/update"
        response = requests.post(dashboard_update_url, json=alert_data)
        if response.status_code != 200:
            raise Exception("Failed to update dashboard.")
```

performance_report.py
```python
'''
Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
'''
import torch
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix
class PerformanceReport:
    def __init__(self, model, dataloader, device='cpu'):
        self.model = model
        self.dataloader = dataloader
        self.device = device
    def evaluate_model(self):
        self.model.to(self.device)
        self.model.eval()
        all_preds = []
        all_labels = []
        with torch.no_grad():
            for data in self.dataloader:
                inputs, labels = data
                inputs, labels = inputs.to(self.device), labels.to(self.device)
                outputs = self.model(inputs)
                _, preds = torch.max(outputs, 1)
                all_preds.extend(preds.cpu().numpy())
                all_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())
        return all_labels, all_preds
    def generate_report(self):
        labels, preds = self.evaluate_model()
        report = classification_report(labels, preds, target_names=['Normal', 'Anomaly'])
        confusion = confusion_matrix(labels, preds)
        return report, confusion
    def save_report(self, filename='performance_report.txt'):
        report, confusion = self.generate_report()
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write("Classification Report:\n")
            f.write(report)
            f.write("\nConfusion Matrix:\n")
            f.write(str(confusion))
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class SurveillanceGUI:
    def __init__(self, video_handler, analyzer, alert_system):
        self.video_handler = video_handler
        self.analyzer = analyzer
        self.alert_system = alert_system
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("AI Surveillance System")
        self.running = False
    def run(self):
        # Create a frame for video display
        video_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        video_frame.pack()
        # Create a label to display video frames
        self.video_label = tk.Label(video_frame)
        self.video_label.pack()
        # Create a frame for controls
        control_frame = tk.Frame(self.root)
        control_frame.pack()
        # Add start and stop buttons
        start_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Start", command=self.start_stream)
        start_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        stop_button = tk.Button(control_frame, text="Stop", command=self.stop_stream)
        stop_button.pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        # Add a text widget to display alerts
        self.alert_text = tk.Text(self.root, height=10, width=50)
        self.alert_text.pack()
        # Start the main loop
        self.root.mainloop()
    def start_stream(self):
        self.running = True
        self.update_frame()
    def stop_stream(self):
        self.running = False
    def update_frame(self):
        if self.running:
            frame = self.video_handler.get_frame()
            # Convert the frame to an image format Tkinter can use
            image = Image.fromarray(frame)
            image = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image)
            self.video_label.config(image=image)
            self.video_label.image = image
            # Analyze the frame
            result = self.analyzer.analyze_frame(frame)
            # Check for anomalies and send alerts if necessary
            if self.is_anomaly(result):
                self.alert_system.send_email("Anomaly Detected", "An anomaly was detected in the video stream.")
                self.alert_system.send_push_notification("Anomaly Detected")
                self.alert_text.insert(tk.END, "Anomaly Detected\n")
            # Schedule the next frame update
            self.root.after(100, self.update_frame)
    def is_anomaly(self, result):
        # Placeholder for anomaly detection logic
        # This should be replaced with actual logic to determine if the result indicates an anomaly
        return result > 0.5
```

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

## 📖 Documentation

Please see [here](https://python.langchain.com) for full documentation on:

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

```markdown
# AI Surveillance Solution

An advanced AI surveillance solution utilizing TensorFlow or PyTorch to process live or recorded RTSP video feeds for behavior analysis. This system identifies anomalies such as loitering or erratic movement and sends alerts via a web dashboard, email, or push notifications. It includes necessary model files, a deployment-ready inference engine in Docker, and a report on performance metrics.

## Main Functions

1. **Video Stream Handling**: Processes live or recorded RTSP video feeds.
2. **Behavior Analysis**: Utilizes a pre-trained model to analyze video frames for anomalies.
3. **Alert System**: Sends notifications via email, push notifications, and updates a web dashboard.
4. **Web Dashboard**: Displays alerts and system status using a Flask application.
5. **Performance Reporting**: Generates a report on the model's performance metrics.
6. **User Interface**: Provides a GUI for user interaction using Tkinter.

## Installation

### Environment Setup

1. **Clone the Repository**: 
   ```bash
   git clone <repository-url>
   cd <repository-directory>
   ```

2. **Install Dependencies**: 
   Ensure you have Python installed, then run:
   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

3. **Docker Setup** (Optional for deployment):
   - Ensure Docker is installed on your system.
   - Build the Docker image:
     ```bash
     docker build -t ai-surveillance .
     ```

## Usage

### Running the Application

1. **Configure the System**:
   - Update `main.py` with your RTSP stream URL and email configurations.

2. **Start the Application**:
   - Run the main script:
     ```bash
     python main.py
     ```

3. **Access the Web Dashboard**:
   - Open your web browser and navigate to `http://localhost:5000` to view the dashboard.

4. **Interact with the GUI**:
   - Use the GUI to start and stop the video stream and view alerts.

### Performance Report

- To generate a performance report, ensure your model and data loader are correctly configured in `performance_report.py`, then run:
  ```bash
  python performance_report.py
  ```
- The report will be saved as `performance_report.txt`.

## Documentation

For detailed documentation on each module and function, refer to the docstrings within the code files. This includes information on parameters, return values, and usage examples.

## Support

For further assistance or to report issues, please contact our support team at support@example.com.

```
